vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.9322em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span>et&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span>roceeds&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>rom&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span>re<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>erence&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">S</span>hares</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.4461em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span>i<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.03588em;">v</span>idend&nbsp;on&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span>re<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>erence&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">S</span>hares</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<h3>Calculation of Cost of Debentures:</h3>
The cost of debentures is the interest expense on debentures divided by the net proceeds from the issuance of debentures.

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>f</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>D</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>I</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>E</mi><mi>x</mi><mi>p</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>e</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>n</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>D</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>t</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>P</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>c</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>d</mi><mi>s</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>f</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>D</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cost \ of \ Debentures = \frac{Interest \ Expense \ on \ Debentures}{Net \ Proceeds \ from \ Debentures}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span>ost&nbsp;o<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>&nbsp;Debentures<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.4133em; vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.9322em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span>et&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span>roceeds&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>rom&nbsp;Debentures</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.4461em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span>nterest&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span>xpense&nbsp;on&nbsp;Debentures</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<h3>Calculation of Cost of Retained Earnings:</h3>
The cost of retained earnings is the opportunity cost, representing the return shareholders could earn on alternative investments of similar risk.

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>f</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>R</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>d</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>E</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>g</mi><mi>s</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>e</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>f</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>R</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>n</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>n</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>C</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>m</mi><mi>p</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>e</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>I</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>v</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>m</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>s</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cost \ of \ Retained \ Earnings = Rate \ of \ Return \ on \ Comparable \ Investments</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span>ost&nbsp;o<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span>etained&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span>a<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span>nin<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03588em;">g</span>s<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span>ate&nbsp;o<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span>etu<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span>n&nbsp;on&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span>ompa<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span>ab<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em;">l</span>e&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span>n<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03588em;">v</span>estments</span></span></span></span>
<h3>Weighted Average Cost of Capital (WACC):</h3><h4>Formula for WACC:</h4>
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mi>E</mi><mi>V</mi></mfrac><mo>×</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mi>P</mi><mi>V</mi></mfrac><mo>×</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>p</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mi>D</mi><mi>V</mi></mfrac><mo>×</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>d</mi></msub><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>T</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = \frac{E}{V} \times r_e + \frac{P}{V} \times r_p + \frac{D}{V} \times r_d \times (1 - T)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2173em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span></span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>e</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2173em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span></span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8694em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>p</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2173em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span></span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>d</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>(1<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>−<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span>)</span></span></span></span>

Where:
<ul><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span></span></span></span></span> = Market value of equity</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">P</span></span></span></span></span> = Market value of preference shares</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">D</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span></span></span></span></span> = Market value of debt</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span></span></span></span></span> = Total market value of the firm (E + P + D)</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r_e</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5806em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>e</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = Cost of equity</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>p</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r_p</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7167em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>p</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = Cost of preference shares</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>d</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r_d</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5806em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>d</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = Cost of debt</li><li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>T</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">T</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span></span></span></span></span> = Corporate tax rate</li></ul><h3>Example Calculation for WACC:</h3>
Let's assume a firm has:
<ul><li>Market value of equity (E) = $50,000</li><li>Market value of preference shares (P) = $10,000</li><li>Market value of debt (D) = $40,000</li><li>Cost of equity (r_e) = 10%</li><li>Cost of preference shares (r_p) = 8%</li><li>Cost of debt (r_d) = 5%</li><li>Corporate tax rate (T) = 25%</li></ul>
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>50</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.10</mn><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>10</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.08</mn><mo>+</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>40</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.05</mn><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>0.25</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = \frac{50,000}{100,000} \times 0.10 + \frac{10,000}{100,000} \times 0.08 + \frac{40,000}{100,000} \times 0.05 \times (1 - 0.25)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3783em; vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8972em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>100,000</span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.4461em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>50,000</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.10<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3783em; vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8972em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>100,000</span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.4461em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>10,000</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.08<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3783em; vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8972em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>100,000</span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.4461em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>40,000</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.05<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>(1<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>−<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>0.25)</span></span></span></span>

Calculating this will give you the Weighted Average Cost of Capital (WACC), which represents the average cost of funds employed by the firm.

**ChatGPT:** <div class="">Sources of Business Finance: Long – Term Sources of Finance – Equity Shares, 
Preference Shares, Debentures and Bonds, explain properly with example. 

**ChatGPT:** <div class="">Sources of Business Finance: Long – Term Sources of Finance – Equity Shares, 
Preference Shares, Debentures and Bonds, explain properly with example. 

**ChatGPT:** 
Certainly! Long-term sources of finance are vital for businesses to fund their operations and growth over an extended period. Here are explanations for some common long-term sources of finance:
<h3>Equity Shares:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Equity shares represent ownership in a company and entitle shareholders to a portion of profits as dividends. Companies issue equity shares to raise capital without incurring debt obligations. Shareholders also have voting rights in company matters.

<strong>Example:</strong> Suppose a company XYZ issues 100,000 shares at $10 per share, raising $1,000,000. Shareholders become partial owners and may receive dividends based on company performance.
<h3>Preference Shares:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Preference shares are a hybrid security with characteristics of both equity and debt. They provide shareholders with fixed dividends before common shareholders and often lack voting rights.

<strong>Example:</strong> Company ABC issues 5,000 preference shares at $100 each, offering a 5% dividend rate. Shareholders receive priority in dividend payments over common shareholders.
<h3>Debentures:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Debentures are long-term debt instruments issued by companies to raise funds from the public. They typically offer fixed interest payments and a repayment of principal amount at maturity.

<strong>Example:</strong> Company LMN issues $500,000 worth of 5-year debentures at 8% interest. Investors receive regular interest payments and get the principal back after five years.
<h3>Bonds:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Bonds are similar to debentures but are usually issued by governments or large corporations. They represent loans made by investors to the issuer in exchange for periodic interest payments and return of principal at maturity.

<strong>Example:</strong> Government issues $1,000,000 worth of 10-year bonds at 4% interest. Investors receive interest payments every six months and get the principal back after ten years.
<h3>Importance:</h3>
Each source of finance has its advantages and considerations:
<ul><li><strong>Equity shares</strong> offer ownership and potential for higher returns but dilute ownership and involve sharing profits.</li><li><strong>Preference shares</strong> offer fixed dividends but don't usually confer voting rights.</li><li><strong>Debentures and bonds</strong> provide fixed-interest financing but require regular interest payments and repayment of principal at maturity.</li></ul>
Businesses often use a mix of these sources to balance costs, risks, and control while meeting their capital requirements for growth and operational needs. Choosing the right mix depends on factors like cost, risk tolerance, and financial goals.

Certainly! Long-term sources of finance are vital for businesses to fund their operations and growth over an extended period. Here are explanations for some common long-term sources of finance:
<h3>Equity Shares:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Equity shares represent ownership in a company and entitle shareholders to a portion of profits as dividends. Companies issue equity shares to raise capital without incurring debt obligations. Shareholders also have voting rights in company matters.

<strong>Example:</strong> Suppose a company XYZ issues 100,000 shares at $10 per share, raising $1,000,000. Shareholders become partial owners and may receive dividends based on company performance.
<h3>Preference Shares:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Preference shares are a hybrid security with characteristics of both equity and debt. They provide shareholders with fixed dividends before common shareholders and often lack voting rights.

<strong>Example:</strong> Company ABC issues 5,000 preference shares at $100 each, offering a 5% dividend rate. Shareholders receive priority in dividend payments over common shareholders.
<h3>Debentures:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Debentures are long-term debt instruments issued by companies to raise funds from the public. They typically offer fixed interest payments and a repayment of principal amount at maturity.

<strong>Example:</strong> Company LMN issues $500,000 worth of 5-year debentures at 8% interest. Investors receive regular interest payments and get the principal back after five years.
<h3>Bonds:</h3>
<strong>Explanation:</strong> Bonds are similar to debentures but are usually issued by governments or large corporations. They represent loans made by investors to the issuer in exchange for periodic interest payments and return of principal at maturity.

<strong>Example:</strong> Government issues $1,000,000 worth of 10-year bonds at 4% interest. Investors receive interest payments every six months and get the principal back after ten years.
<h3>Importance:</h3>
Each source of finance has its advantages and considerations:
<ul><li><strong>Equity shares</strong> offer ownership and potential for higher returns but dilute ownership and involve sharing profits.</li><li><strong>Preference shares</strong> offer fixed dividends but don't usually confer voting rights.</li><li><strong>Debentures and bonds</strong> provide fixed-interest financing but require regular interest payments and repayment of principal at maturity.</li></ul>
Businesses often use a mix of these sources to balance costs, risks, and control while meeting their capital requirements for growth and operational needs. Choosing the right mix depends on factors like cost, risk tolerance, and financial goals.

Operating Income Approach (NOI), Traditional and Modigliani Miller Approach, explain with example if they have formula explain that too. 

**ChatGPT:** 
Certainly! The capital structure decision refers to the composition of a company's financial resources, specifically the mix of equity and debt used to finance its operations. Several approaches are used to determine the optimal capital structure:
<h3>1. Net Income Approach (NI):</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The Net Income Approach suggests that the cost of debt is lower than the cost of equity due to the tax-deductibility of interest expenses. Thus, maximizing debt in the capital structure increases interest tax shields, which ultimately maximizes the firm's value.

<strong>Formula:</strong> The cost of equity (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r_e</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5806em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>e</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>) and the cost of debt (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>d</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r_d</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5806em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>d</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>) are calculated separately. The weighted average cost of capital (WACC) is computed considering the proportion of equity and debt in the capital structure.
<h3>2. Net Operating Income Approach (NOI):</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The Net Operating Income Approach assumes that the overall cost of capital remains constant within a certain range of debt-to-equity ratios. It proposes that the WACC remains unchanged irrespective of the changes in the capital structure until a certain level, after which it increases.

<strong>Formula:</strong> Similar to the Net Income Approach, the WACC is calculated by determining the cost of equity and debt separately and then computing the weighted average.
<h3>3. Traditional Approach:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The Traditional Approach focuses on the trade-off between the cost and the risk associated with various financing options. It suggests that there exists an optimal capital structure that minimizes the firm's overall cost of capital.

<strong>Example:</strong> Let's consider a company with the following capital structure:
<ul><li>Equity: $500,000 with a cost of equity of 12%.</li><li>Debt: $300,000 with a cost of debt of 6%.</li><li>Tax rate: 30%.</li></ul>
<strong>Calculations:</strong>
<ol><li>Calculate the weighted average cost of capital (WACC):
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mi>E</mi><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>D</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi></msub><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mi>D</mi><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>D</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>d</mi></msub><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>T</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = \left(\frac{E}{E + D}\times r_e\right) + \left(\frac{D}{E + D}\times r_d \times (1 - T)\right)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2757em; vertical-align: -0.4033em;"></span><span class="minner"><span class="mopen delimcenter" style="top: 0em;">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span>+<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span></span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4033em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.12</mn><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>0.30</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = \left(\frac{500,000}{500,000 + 300,000} \times 0.12\right) + \left(\frac{300,000}{500,000 + 300,000} \times 0.06 \times (1 - 0.30)\right)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.8em; <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0.5</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.12</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0.3</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.70</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>0.0126</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>0.0726</mn><mtext>&nbsp;or&nbsp;</mtext><mn>7.26</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = (0.5 \times 0.12) + (0.3 \times 0.06 \times 0.70) = 0.06 + 0.0126 = 0.0726 \text{ or } 7.26%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>(0.3<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.06<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>0.70)<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.06<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span>0.0126<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span>0.0726&nbsp;or&nbsp;7.26</span></span></span></span></li></ol><h3>4. Modigliani-Miller (MM) Approach:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The MM Approach, proposed by Modigliani and Miller, suggests that in a perfect market without taxes, capital structure does not affect the firm's value. However, in the real world, taxes, bankruptcy costs, and other factors influence the optimal capital structure.

The MM Approach provides two propositions:
<ul><li>Proposition I: Without taxes, the value of a firm is independent of its capital structure.</li><li>Proposition II: With taxes, the value of a leveraged firm is higher due to the tax shield on debt interest.</li></ul>
These approaches offer different perspectives on the impact of capital structure on a firm's value, considering factors like taxes, costs, and risk. They aid in understanding the optimal mix of debt and equity to maximize a company's value and performance.

<h3>1. Net Income Approach (NI):</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The Net Income Approach suggests that the cost of debt is lower than the cost of equity due to the tax-deductibility of interest expenses. Thus, maximizing debt in the capital structure increases interest tax shields, which ultimately maximizes the firm's value.

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.12</mn><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>×</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>×</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>0.30</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = \left(\frac{500,000}{500,000 + 300,000} \times 0.12\right) + \left(\frac{300,000}{500,000 + 300,000} \times 0.06 \times (1 - 0.30)\right)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.8em; <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mi>A</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0.5</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.12</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0.3</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>0.70</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mn>0.06</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>0.0126</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>0.0726</mn><mtext>&nbsp;or&nbsp;</mtext><mn>7.26</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">WACC = (0.5 \times 0.12) + (0.3 \times 0.06 \times 0.70) = 0.06 + 0.0126 = 0.0726 \text{ or } 7.26%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">W</span>A<span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">CC</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>(0.5<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>0.12)<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>(0.3<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.06<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span>0.70)<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span>0.06<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>+<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span>0.0126<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span>0.0726&nbsp;or&nbsp;7.26</span></span></span></span></li></ol><h3>4. Modigliani-Miller (MM) Approach:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> The MM Approach, proposed by Modigliani and Miller, suggests that in a perfect market without taxes, capital structure does not affect the firm's value. However, in the real world, taxes, bankruptcy costs, and other factors influence the optimal capital structure.

The MM Approach provides two propositions:
<ul><li>Proposition I: Without taxes, the value of a firm is independent of its capital structure.</li><li>Proposition II: With taxes, the value of a leveraged firm is higher due to the tax shield on debt interest.</li></ul>
These approaches offer different perspectives on the impact of capital structure on a firm's value, considering factors like taxes, costs, and risk. They aid in understanding the optimal mix of debt and equity to maximize a company's value and performance.

and Indifference Points, explain with example and formula. 

**ChatGPT:** <div class="">Leverage Analysis – Financial, Operating and Combined Leverage; EBIT-EPS Analysis 
and Indifference Points, explain with example and formula. 

**ChatGPT:** 
Certainly! Leverage refers to the use of fixed-cost funds, such as debt, to increase returns to shareholders when the firm performs well. There are three types of leverage: financial, operating, and combined.
<h3>1. Financial Leverage:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> Financial leverage refers to the use of debt to increase the returns to equity shareholders. It magnifies the effect of changes in earnings before interest and taxes (EBIT) on earnings per share (EPS).
<p><strong>Formula:</strong> The formula for financial leverage is:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>F</mi><mi>L</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><mi>T</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>T</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">FL = \frac{EBIT}{EBT}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">F</span>L<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2173em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">EBT</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span></span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p><h3>2. Operating Leverage:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> Operating leverage arises from the use of fixed operating costs in a company's cost structure. It magnifies the effect of changes in sales on EBIT.
<p><strong>Formula:</strong> The formula for operating leverage is:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>O</mi><mi>L</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>S</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>V</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>C</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>s</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><mi>T</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">OL = \frac{Sales - Variable Costs}{EBIT}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">O</span>L<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2251em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8801em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">S</span>a<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.01968em;">l</span>es−Va<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">r</span>iab<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.01968em;">l</span>e<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span>osts</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p><h3>3. Combined Leverage:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> Combined leverage is the result of the combination of financial leverage and operating leverage. It magnifies the effect of changes in sales on EPS.
<p><strong>Formula:</strong> The formula for combined leverage is:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><mi>L</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>F</mi><mi>L</mi><mo>×</mo><mi>O</mi><mi>L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">CL = FL \times OL</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span>L<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">F</span>L<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span>×<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">O</span>L</span></span></span></span></p><h3>EBIT-EPS Analysis and Indifference Points:</h3>
<strong>Concept:</strong> EBIT-EPS analysis helps in determining the impact of different capital structures on earnings per share (EPS) at various levels of EBIT. Indifference points are the EBIT levels where two different financing plans result in the same EPS.
<p><strong>Formula:</strong> The formula to calculate EPS is:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>P</mi><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><mi>T</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>I</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>m</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>f</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>S</mi><mi>h</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">EPS = \frac{EBIT - Interest}{Number \ of \ Shares}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">EPS</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3534em; vertical-align: -0.4811em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8723em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span>umb<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">er</span>&nbsp;o<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">S</span>hares</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span>−<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span>nterest</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4811em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<strong>Example:</strong> Let's consider a company with two financing plans:
<ul><li>Plan A: $500,000 debt at 6% interest rate.</li><li>Plan B: $300,000 debt at 8% interest rate.</li></ul>
Assuming the company has 100,000 shares outstanding and a tax rate of 30%.

<strong>Calculations:</strong>
<ol><li><p>Calculate EBIT at the indifference point:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><mi>T</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>I</mi><mi>n</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>t</mi><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>N</mi><mi>u</mi><mi>m</mi><mi>b</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>o</mi><mi>f</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>S</mi><mi>h</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>s</mi><mo>×</mo><mi>E</mi><mi>P</mi><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>T</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>x</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi>R</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>e</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">EBIT = \frac{Interest + (Number \ of \ Shares \times EPS)}{1 - Tax \ Rate}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.4133em; vertical-align: -0.4033em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.01em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1−<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span>ax&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span>ate</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.485em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span>nterest+(<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span>umb<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">er</span>&nbsp;o<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span>&nbsp;<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">S</span>hares×<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">EPS</span>)</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4033em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>
For Plan A:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><msub><mi>T</mi><mi>A</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>0.06</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>500</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>×</mo><mi>E</mi><mi>P</mi><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>0.70</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">EBIT_A = \frac{0.06 \times 500,000 + (100,000 \times EPS)}{0.70}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3283em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.1389em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span>A</span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span>=<span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.355em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.01em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span>0.70</span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.485em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0.06×500,000+(100,000×<span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">EPS</span>)</span></span></span></span>​</span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p><p>For Plan B:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>I</mi><msub><mi>T</mi><mi>B</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>0.08</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>300</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn><mo>×</mo><mi>E</mi><mi>P</mi><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>0.70</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">EBIT_B = \frac{0.08 \times 300,000 + (100,000 \times EPS)}{0.70}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05017em;">EB</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3283em;"><span style="top: -2.55em;
